This is becoming a full-scale **Tactical Asset Manager**. By moving from static strings to a file-based arsenal, you're essentially building a "Loadout" system for your AI agents.

Here is the **Battle Plan** for the Prompt Arsenal:

### 1. The "Tactical Loadout" UI (Per Node)
*   **Two-Stage Dropdown:** Next to the Model Picker, a "Mission Profile" picker.
*   **Visual State:** The dropdown shows the active prompt (e.g., `eagle_v21_standard`).
*   **The "Manage" Trigger:** An icon (maybe a wrench or a crosshair) that opens the **Arsenal Command Center** modal.

### 2. The Arsenal Command Center (The Deep Work)
This is where the management happens. Instead of just a text box, we build a **Workbench**:
*   **Browser Pane (Left):** A list of all `.md` files in that phase's directory.
*   **The Editor (Center):** High-density mono-font editor for the prompt.
*   **Action HUD (Right/Top):**
    *   **[LOCK DEFAULT]:** Saves the filename to the DB as the "Auto-Arm" choice for that stage.
    *   **[CLONE]:** Creates `filename_COPY.md` and opens it.
    *   **[PURGE]:** Deletes the file (with a red confirmation flash).
    *   **[NEW ASSET]:** Starts a blank slate.
    *   **[PREVIEW]:** A "Split View" showing how the prompt looks with dummy data injected into the `{input}` or `{skeleton}` tags.

### 3. The Backend "Armory" (server.ts)
*   **Dir Watching:** The server ensures those 5 directories exist on boot.
*   **File I/O:** Real-time reading/writing to `/home/flintx/peacock/prompts/[phase]/`.
*   **The "Default" Logic:** When the UI asks for "Spark's Prompts," the server sends the list, but the UI checks its local memory (Dexie) to see which one was marked as the "Default Loadout."

### 4. Casino Doctrine Integration
*   **Cloning:** Play a mechanical "re-chambering" sound. Text descrambles: `DNA_REPLICATED`.
*   **Saving:** Blinding white flash (100ms) + `ASSET_SECURED`.
*   **Deleting:** Red border vibration + `PURGE_COMPLETE`.

**The Strategic Advantage:**
This allows you to have a "Code-Heavy" Eagle and a "Docs-Heavy" Eagle, and you just swap the "Loadout" based on the mission.

I need to clarify one thing based on your "Final Orders" in the Manifesto: 

You mentioned: *"Every run is a 'Session.' Saved in a DB. I need to be able to wipe specific phases to re-run them without killing the whole session."*

However, you just said: *"each time a phase is activated .. a new session is created."*

**Let's sync on the logic here:**
1.  **The "Grand Session" (The Op):** You start a new operation (e.g., `OP_DRAGON`). This holds the whole Spark -> Falcon -> Eagle -> Owl -> Hawk chain.
2.  **The "Phase Activation":** When you hit "Strike" on Spark, it saves the result. If you then move to Falcon and hit "Strike," does that **update** the current session, or does it **spawn a completely new session ID** in the database so you have a historical trail of every single individual hit?

If it's the latter, then the "Sessions" rail on the left would show every single strike ever made as its own entry. If it's the former, it shows one entry per "Project" or "Run."

**Which route are we taking?**
*   **A:** One Session ID for the whole chain (Spark through Hawk).
*   **B:** Every single "Strike" generates a brand new unique Session/Entry in the DB for maximum auditability.

LOCKED IN. **1 Session = 1 Project.** 

The "Session" is the container for the entire war operation. 

### The "Session Life-Cycle" Protocol:

**1. The Genesis:**
*   You click "NEW_WAR_OP" or load a file from the `start` rail. 
*   A **Unique Session ID** is generated (e.g., `OP_20260114_1430`).
*   The system initializes a blank slate for all 5 phases (Spark -> Hawk).

**2. The Chronological Rail (The Archive):**
*   The "Sessions" tab on the left rail lists every operation in reverse-chrono order.
*   **Visual Intel:** Each session entry in the rail shows:
    *   The Name (e.g., "Build_Auth_Module").
    *   The Timestamp.
    *   **Progress Pips:** 5 small icons/dots representing [S][F][E][O][H]. If Spark and Falcon are done, those dots are green. This lets you see at a glance how far you got in each project.

**3. The "State Restore" Logic:**
*   Clicking a session in the rail **instantly re-hydrates** the entire dashboard.
*   The Mind Map lines, the inputs, the outputs, and even the "Strike Report" stats are all pulled from the DB. 
*   You can jump back into an operation from 3 days ago and finish the Eagle or Owl phase immediately.

**4. The Intra-Session "Wipe" (Precision Reset):**
*   If you are in a session and you hate the Falcon output, you hit the "WIPE" button on the Falcon node.
*   **Behavior:** It clears Falcon's data, but **keeps Spark's output** (the input for Falcon) and keeps the Session ID. It resets the "kill chain" from that point forward without you having to start a brand new project.

**5. Verification (The Handshake):**
*   Before any data is written to the DB, it passes through the **Verbatim CLI**.
*   You see: `[DATABASE] SAVING_STATE :: SESSION_ID: OP_123 :: STAGE: SPARK :: STATUS: SUCCESS`.

# ğŸ§  PEACOCK ENGINE (AI-HANDLER)
**Headless AI Orchestrator & Key Rotator**

## ğŸ’€ THE MISSION
The central nervous system. It decouples the UI from the API keys. It handles the "dirty work" of contacting Google Gemini, Groq, Mistral, and Deepseek, managing rate limits, and normalizing responses.

## ğŸ—ï¸ ARCHITECTURE
*   **Runtime:** Node.js (TypeScript) + Express.
*   **Security:** `KeyManager.ts` implements Round-Robin key rotation.
*   **Storage:** Local Filesystem access for "Ammo" (Context files) and "Prompts".

## ğŸš€ PROTOCOLS
### 1. Ignite Engine
`npm run dev`
*Port:* `8888`

## ğŸ› ï¸ FEATURES
*   **Universal Striker:** Single endpoint (`/v1/strike`) for all models.
*   **Key Pools:** Automatic failover if a key is rate-limited.
*   **Model Registry:** Centralized configuration for model Tiers (Cheap vs Expensive).

âœ¦ ğŸ§  PEACOCK ENGINE (AI-HANDLER) // OPERATIONAL MANUAL

  The Peacock Engine is a headless, high-performance gateway designed to orchestrate strikes across multiple LLM providers while
  serving as a secure bridge to your local filesystem. It is the "Nervous System" that powers the Peacock V21 HUD.

  ---

  1. CORE ARCHITECTURE
   * Host: http://localhost:8888
   * Version: v1
   * Tech Stack: Node.js, Express, TypeScript, Axios.
   * Security: Handles key rotation and proxying internally so the frontend stays clean and air-gapped from direct API keys.

  ---

  2. API ENDPOINTS

  A. Intelligence Strikes
  POST /v1/strike
  Executes a prompt against a specific model node.
   * Payload:

   1     {
   2       "modelId": "gemini-2.0-flash",
   3       "prompt": "Your strategic payload here...",
   4       "temp": 0.7
   5     }
   * Response:
   1     { "content": "The generated output..." }

  B. Node Registry
  GET /v1/models
  Retrieves the full tactical arsenal of available models, their tiers, and operational notes.

  C. Filesystem Bridge (Ammo & Prompts)
  The engine has direct access to your local directories to bypass browser security.

   * List Ammo: GET /v1/fs/ammo -> Returns filenames from /home/flintx/ammo.
   * Read Ammo: GET /v1/fs/ammo/:filename -> Returns the text content of a specific file.
   * List Prompts: GET /v1/fs/prompts -> Returns all .md protocols from /home/flintx/prompts.
   * Sync Prompt: POST /v1/fs/prompts -> Saves a modified protocol directly to disk.

  ---

  3. KEY ROTATION & PROXIES
  The engine automatically manages:
   * Ammo Shuffling: It pulls from a deck of keys (e.g., GOOGLE_KEYS, GROQ_KEYS) defined in your environment.
   * Proxy Tunneling: If PROXY_ENABLED=true, all strikes are routed through your defined PROXY_URL to ensure anonymity and
     bypass regional rate limits.

  ---

  4. OPERATIONAL WORKFLOW (The "Ritual")
   1. Boot: Ensure your environment is loaded and run npm run dev in the /ai-handler directory.
   2. Strike: The Peacock HUD sends a POST request to /strike.
   3. Sync: The Engine contacts the provider (Groq/Google/etc.), rotates the key if necessary, and streams the result back to
      the HUD.
   4. Vault: The result is simultaneously synced to your local filesystem via the /fs routes.

  ---

  5. ENVIRONMENT SETUP
  Ensure your ~/.env.global or local .env contains:
   * GOOGLE_KEYS: Comma-separated list of Gemini keys.
   * GROQ_KEYS: Comma-separated list of Groq keys.
   * DEEPSEEK_KEYS / MISTRAL_KEYS: Respective provider keys.
   * PROXY_URL: (Optional) Your proxy endpoint.

  STATUS: âš¡ ENGINE ACTIVE ON PORT 8888. Ready for Strike.

----------------------------------------

# ğŸ§  PEACOCK ENGINE
**Headless AI Orchestrator**

## MISSION
To serve as the central nervous system for all FlintX AI operations. It handles key rotation, proxy routing, and API normalization.

## SETUP
1.  Ensure `~/.env.global` is loaded in your shell.
2.  Run `npm install`.
3.  Run `npm run dev`.

## ENDPOINTS
*   `POST /v1/strike`: Execute a prompt.
*   `GET /v1/models`: Get available models.


EOF

# ğŸ§  PEACOCK ENGINE
**Headless AI Orchestrator**

## MISSION
To serve as the central nervous system for all FlintX AI operations. It handles key rotation, proxy routing, and API normalization.

## SETUP
1.  Ensure `~/.env.global` is loaded in your shell.
2.  Run `npm install`.
3.  Run `npm run dev`.

## ENDPOINTS
*   `POST /v1/strike`: Execute a prompt.
*   `GET /v1/models`: Get available models.


EOF

# ğŸ§  PEACOCK ENGINE
**Headless AI Orchestrator**

## MISSION
To serve as the central nervous system for all FlintX AI operations. It handles key rotation, proxy routing, and API normalization.

## SETUP
1.  Ensure `~/.env.global` is loaded in your shell.
2.  Run `npm install`.
3.  Run `npm run dev`.

## ENDPOINTS
*   `POST /v1/strike`: Execute a prompt.
*   `GET /v1/models`: Get available models.


EOF

â–ˆâ–ˆâ•—   â–ˆâ–ˆâ•—â–ˆâ–ˆâ–ˆâ–ˆâ–ˆâ–ˆâ–ˆâ•—â–ˆâ–ˆâ–ˆâ–ˆâ–ˆâ–ˆâ–ˆâ•—â–ˆâ–ˆâ–ˆâ–ˆâ–ˆâ–ˆâ•—

 â•šâ•â•â•â•â•â• â•šâ•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•šâ•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•šâ•â•  â•šâ•â•

export interface KeyAsset {
  label: string;
  account: string;
  key: string;
}

class KeyPool {
  private deck: KeyAsset[] = [];
  private pointer: number = 0;
  private type: string;

  constructor(envString: string | undefined, type: string) {
    this.type = type;
    if (!envString) {
      console.warn(`\x1b[33m[âš ï¸] NO KEYS LOADED FOR ${type}\x1b[0m`);
      return;
    }

    const entries = envString.split(',');
    entries.forEach((entry, idx) => {
      let label = "";
      let key = "";
      
      if (entry.includes(':')) {
        const parts = entry.split(':');
        label = parts[0];
        key = parts[1];
      } else {
        label = `${type}_DEALER_${String(idx + 1).padStart(2, '0')}`;
        key = entry;
      }
      
      this.deck.push({ 
        label: label.trim(), 
        account: label.trim(), 
        key: key.trim() 
      });
    });
    this.shuffle();
  }

  private shuffle() {
    if (this.deck.length === 0) return;
    console.log(`\n\x1b[1;33m[ğŸ²] ${this.type} DECK SHUFFLING...\x1b[0m`);
    for (let i = this.deck.length - 1; i > 0; i--) {
      const j = Math.floor(Math.random() * (i + 1));
      [this.deck[i], this.deck[j]] = [this.deck[j], this.deck[i]];
    }
    this.pointer = 0;
  }

  public getNext(): KeyAsset {
    if (this.deck.length === 0) throw new Error(`NO AMMUNITION FOR ${this.type}`);
    const asset = this.deck[this.pointer];
    this.pointer++;
    if (this.pointer >= this.deck.length) this.shuffle();
    return asset;
  }

  public dump() {
    console.log(`\n\x1b[1;35m--- [ ${this.type} ARSENAL LOADED ] ---\x1b[0m`);
    this.deck.forEach((a, i) => {
        const masked = a.key.length > 8 ? `${a.key.substring(0, 8)}...` : 'INVALID';
        console.log(`[${String(i+1).padStart(2,'0')}] \x1b[1;92m${a.account.padEnd(20)}\x1b[0m | ID: ${masked}`);
    });
  }
}

// Load pools from Environment Variables
export const GroqPool = new KeyPool(process.env.GROQ_KEYS, 'GROQ');
export const GooglePool = new KeyPool(process.env.GOOGLE_KEYS, 'GOOGLE');
export const DeepSeekPool = new KeyPool(process.env.DEEPSEEK_KEYS, 'DEEPSEEK');
export const MistralPool = new KeyPool(process.env.MISTRAL_KEYS, 'MISTRAL');

GroqPool.dump();
GooglePool.dump();
DeepSeekPool.dump();
MistralPool.dump();

import axios from 'axios';
import { GoogleGenAI } from '@google/genai';
import { GroqPool, GooglePool, DeepSeekPool, MistralPool } from './KeyManager';
import { HttpsProxyAgent } from 'https-proxy-agent';

const proxyUrl = process.env.PROXY_URL;
const agent = (process.env.PROXY_ENABLED === 'true' && proxyUrl) ? new HttpsProxyAgent(proxyUrl) : null;

export const executeStrike = async (gateway: string, modelId: string, prompt: string, temp: number) => {
  if (gateway === 'groq') {
    const asset = GroqPool.getNext();
    console.log(`[ğŸ’¥ STRIKE] ACC: ${asset.account.padEnd(15)} | GW: GROQ`);
    try {
      const response = await axios.post('https://api.groq.com/openai/v1/chat/completions', {
        model: modelId, messages: [{ role: 'user', content: prompt }], temperature: temp
      }, { httpsAgent: agent, headers: { 'Authorization': `Bearer ${asset.key}` } });
      return { content: response.data.choices[0].message.content, keyUsed: asset.account };
    } catch (e: any) { const err: any = new Error(e.message); err.keyUsed = asset.account; throw err; }
  }
  if (gateway === 'deepseek') {
    const asset = DeepSeekPool.getNext();
    console.log(`[ğŸ’¥ STRIKE] ACC: ${asset.account.padEnd(15)} | GW: DEEPSEEK`);
    try {
      const response = await axios.post('https://api.deepseek.com/chat/completions', {
        model: modelId, messages: [{ role: 'user', content: prompt }], temperature: temp, stream: false
      }, { httpsAgent: agent, headers: { 'Authorization': `Bearer ${asset.key}`, 'Content-Type': 'application/json' } });
      return { content: response.data.choices[0].message.content, keyUsed: asset.account };
    } catch (e: any) { const err: any = new Error(e.message); err.keyUsed = asset.account; throw err; }
  }
  if (gateway === 'mistral') {
    const asset = MistralPool.getNext();
    console.log(`[ğŸ’¥ STRIKE] ACC: ${asset.account.padEnd(15)} | GW: MISTRAL`);
    try {
      const response = await axios.post('https://api.mistral.ai/v1/chat/completions', {
        model: modelId, messages: [{ role: 'user', content: prompt }], temperature: temp
      }, { httpsAgent: agent, headers: { 'Authorization': `Bearer ${asset.key}`, 'Content-Type': 'application/json' } });
      return { content: response.data.choices[0].message.content, keyUsed: asset.account };
    } catch (e: any) { const err: any = new Error(e.message); err.keyUsed = asset.account; throw err; }
  }
  if (gateway === 'google') {
    const asset = GooglePool.getNext();
    console.log(`[ğŸ’¥ STRIKE] ACC: ${asset.account.padEnd(15)} | GW: GOOGLE`);
    const ai = new GoogleGenAI({ apiKey: asset.key });
    try {
      const result = await ai.models.generateContent({
        model: modelId,
        contents: [{ parts: [{ text: prompt }] }],
        config: { temperature: temp }
      });
      // In @google/genai, the output is in result.text
      const output = result.text || '';
      if (!output) throw new Error('STRIKE RETURNED NULL CONTENT');
      return { content: output, keyUsed: asset.account };
    } catch (error: any) {
      const err: any = new Error(error.message);
      err.keyUsed = asset.account;
      throw err;
    }
  }
  throw new Error(`Gateway ${gateway} not supported`);
};

import { Router } from 'express';
import fs from 'fs/promises';
import path from 'path';

export const fsRouter = Router();

const AMMO_DIR = '/home/flintx/ammo';
const PROMPTS_DIR = '/home/flintx/prompts';

fsRouter.get('/ammo', async (req, res) => {
  try {
    const files = await fs.readdir(AMMO_DIR);
    res.json(files.filter(f => f.endsWith('.md') || f.endsWith('.txt') || f.endsWith('.json')));
  } catch (e) { res.status(500).json({ error: 'Failed to read ammo dir' }); }
});

fsRouter.get('/ammo/:file', async (req, res) => {
  try {
    const content = await fs.readFile(path.join(AMMO_DIR, req.params.file), 'utf-8');
    res.json({ content });
  } catch (e) { res.status(500).json({ error: 'Failed to read file' }); }
});

fsRouter.get('/prompts', async (req, res) => {
  try {
    const files = await fs.readdir(PROMPTS_DIR);
    const prompts = await Promise.all(files.filter(f => f.endsWith('.md')).map(async f => ({
      id: f.replace('.md', ''),
      content: await fs.readFile(path.join(PROMPTS_DIR, f), 'utf-8')
    })));
    res.json(prompts);
  } catch (e) { res.status(500).json({ error: 'Failed to read prompts' }); }
});

fsRouter.post('/prompts', async (req, res) => {
  const { id, content } = req.body;
  try {
    await fs.writeFile(path.join(PROMPTS_DIR, `${id}.md`), content);
    res.json({ status: 'SAVED' });
  } catch (e) { res.status(500).json({ error: 'Failed to save prompt' }); }
});

 â•šâ•â•â•â•â•â• â•šâ•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•šâ•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•šâ•â•  â•šâ•â•

import { Router } from 'express';
import { executeStrike } from '../core/striker';
import { MODEL_REGISTRY } from '../config/modelRegistry';

export const strikeRouter = Router();

strikeRouter.post('/', async (req, res) => {
  const { modelId, prompt, temp = 0.7 } = req.body;
  
  const modelConfig = MODEL_REGISTRY.find(m => m.id === modelId);
  if (!modelConfig) return res.status(400).json({ error: 'Unknown Model ID' });

  try {
    const result = await executeStrike(modelConfig.gateway, modelId, prompt, temp);
    res.json({ content: result.content, keyUsed: result.keyUsed });
  } catch (error: any) {
    res.status(500).json({ error: error.message, keyUsed: error.keyUsed || 'DEALER_FAILED' });
  }
});

 â•šâ•â•â•â•â•â• â•šâ•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•šâ•â•â•â•â•â•â•â•šâ•â•  â•šâ•â•

import 'dotenv/config'; 
import express from 'express';
import cors from 'cors';
import { strikeRouter } from './routes/strike';
import { modelsRouter } from './routes/models';
import fs from 'fs';
import path from 'path';

const app = express();
const PORT = 8888;

app.use(cors());
app.use(express.json({ limit: '50mb' }));

// --- SYSTEM STRIKE ROUTES ---
app.use('/v1/strike', strikeRouter);
app.use('/v1/models', modelsRouter);

// --- PEACOCK V22 START RAIL ---
const START_DIR = '/home/flintx/peacock/start';

app.get('/v1/fs/start', (req, res) => {
  try {
    if (!fs.existsSync(START_DIR)) {
      return res.json([]);
    }
    // Show all non-hidden files
    const files = fs.readdirSync(START_DIR).filter(f => !f.startsWith('.'));
    res.json(files);
  } catch (err: any) {
    res.status(500).json({ error: err.message });
  }
});

app.get('/v1/fs/start/:name', (req, res) => {
  try {
    const filePath = path.join(START_DIR, req.params.name);
    if (!fs.existsSync(filePath)) {
      return res.status(404).send("File not found");
    }
    res.json({ content: fs.readFileSync(filePath, 'utf-8') });
  } catch (err: any) {
    res.status(500).json({ error: err.message });
  }
});

// --- LEGACY PROMPTS ENDPOINT ---
const PROMPTS_DIR = '/home/flintx/peacock/nexus.prompts';

app.get('/v1/fs/prompts', (req, res) => {
  try {
    if (!fs.existsSync(PROMPTS_DIR)) return res.json([]);
    const files = fs.readdirSync(PROMPTS_DIR).filter(f => f.endsWith('.md') || f.endsWith('.txt'));
    const prompts = files.map(f => ({
      id: path.parse(f).name,
      content: fs.readFileSync(path.join(PROMPTS_DIR, f), 'utf-8')
    }));
    res.json(prompts);
  } catch (err: any) {
    res.status(500).json({ error: err.message });
  }
});

app.get('/health', (req, res) => {
  res.json({ status: 'ONLINE', system: 'PEACOCK_ENGINE_V22' });
});

app.listen(PORT, () => {
  console.log(`âš¡ PEACOCK OMEGA ENGINE ACTIVE ON PORT ${PORT}`);
  console.log(`   - Start Rail Target: ${START_DIR}`);
});

we want to make this app look like this. # ğŸ’€ PEACOCK: VISUAL DOCTRINE & UX GUIDE
**STYLE:** HIGH-STAKES CASINO / MILITARY HUD
**PALETTE:** #050505 (VOID), #00FF41 (MATRIX), #FFD700 (VOLTAGE)

---

## 1. GLOBAL PHYSICS (ANIMATION)
*   **No Fading:** Things do not "fade in." They **DESCRAMBLE** (Matrix text effect) or **SLIDE** (Mechanical insertion).
*   **Tension:** While processing, lines and borders must **VIBRATE** (x: -1, x: 1 loop) to show engine stress.
*   **Release:** Upon success, the UI **FLASHES WHITE** (100ms) and plays a `click_latch.mp3` sound.

## 2. COMPONENT STYLING

### **A. The Mind Map (Top Pane)**
*   **Visual:** SVG Nodes connected by "Laser Lines."
*   **Behavior:**
    *   *Idle:* Dim Green opacity 0.3.
    *   *Active:* Bright Yellow, pulsing line width (1px to 3px).
    *   *Success:* Solid Neon Green. "Data Packet" dot travels the line.

### **B. The Nerve Center (Bottom Console)**
*   **Style:** CRT Terminal. Scanline overlay (`pointer-events-none`).
*   **Typography:** `JetBrains Mono`. Glow effect (`text-shadow: 0 0 5px #00FF41`).
*   **Behavior:** Auto-scrolls to bottom.

### **C. The Tactical Flyout (Settings)**
*   **Transition:** `transform: translateX(100%)` to `0%`.
*   **Speed:** Instant (Type: Spring, Stiffness: 300).
*   **Glass:** Background `rgba(10, 10, 10, 0.95)` with `backdrop-filter: blur(10px)`.

### **D. The "Jackpot"**
*   **Trigger:** All stages complete.
*   **Effect:**
    *   Background flashes Green (opacity 0.1).
    *   Center Text: "SEQUENCE COMPLETE" descrambles.
    *   Border: Running ants animation turns solid.

---

*   `fonts/JetBrainsMono-Bold.ttf`
*   `sounds/mechanical_latch.mp3`
*   `sounds/turbine_hum.mp3`
*   `images/peacock_logo_matrix.png`

This is a **high-fidelity psychological upgrade.** By combining the industrial weight of a **Military HUD** with the dopamine loops of a **High-Stakes Casino**, you are moving from a "tool" to a "ritual." 

Here is my breakdown of the **Doctrine**:

### 1. The "Anti-Vibe" Physics (Animations)
The decision to **ban fading** is the most important part of this guide. Fading is "soft." **Descrambling** and **Sliding** are "mechanical." It reinforces the idea that the app isn't "thinking"â€”it's **calculating.** 
*   **Engine Stress (Vibrate):** This is genius for UX. Usually, users hate waiting for AI. By making the UI vibrate, you turn the "wait" into a "build-up of power." The user isn't waiting for a slow API; they are watching a reactor charge up.

### 2. The Mind Map (Laser Lines & Packets)
*   The "Data Packet" dot traveling the line is the perfect visual for the **Guided Strike Path**. 
*   It physically shows the handoff: *Spark just delivered the payload, and you are literally watching it travel into Falcon's chamber.* It makes the sequence feel unstoppable.

### 3. The Nerve Center (CRT Aesthetic)
*   **Scanlines + Glow:** This creates the "Zero-Cool" hacker atmosphere.
*   **Auto-scroll:** Essential for the "Verbatim CLI" we planned. It needs to feel like a live data-stream from a satellite.

### 4. The "Jackpot" (The Climax)
*   This is your **Loom Video money shot.** 
*   When that final HAWK strike hits and the "Running Ants" border turns solid while the screen flashesâ€”thatâ€™s the moment the viewer realizes the project is **Done.** Itâ€™s the visual "Drop" in a song.

### 5. Tactical Asset Readiness
*   **Audio is Key:** The `mechanical_latch.mp3` and `turbine_hum.mp3` will do 50% of the work. If it *sounds* like heavy machinery, it *feels* like a heavy strike.

**My Verdict:** 
This is **aggressive, professional, and addictive.** It moves the "NFL Playoff Bracket" into a dark, high-tech war room. It fits the "Architect Trevino" persona perfectly.

**Ready to move into the implementation phase?** I can start with the **Global CSS (Scanlines/Vibrations)** and the **SVG Laser Line logic**.
